This is surprisingly tricky, because of\n308: \t// various contextual defaults and/or checking the user has access to the model, etc.\n309: \tproviderConfig, modelConfig, err := resolveRequestedModel(ctx, h.logger, currentModelConfig, h.feature, request, h.getModel)\n310: \tif err != nil {\n311: \t\t// NOTE: We return the raw error to the user assuming that it contains relevant\n312: \t\t// user-facing diagnostic information, and doesn't leak any internal details.\n313: \t\th.logger.Error(\"error resolving model\", log.Error(err))\n314: \t\treturn &errcode.HTTPErr{\n315: \t\t\tStatus: http.StatusBadRequest,\n316: \t\t\tErr:    err,\n317: \t\t}\n318: \t}\n319: \n320: \t// ensure that all features of the request (i.e. vision, tool use, etc.) are\n321: \t// supported by the requested model\n322: \tif err := validateRequestCapabilities(request, params, modelConfig, h.logger, h.feature, h.scope); err != nil {\n323: \t\treturn err\n324: \t}\n325: \n326: \tctx, done := Trace(ctx, string(h.scope), modelConfig.ModelName, request.MaxTokensToSample).\n327: \t\tWithErrorP(&err).\n328: \t\tBuild()\n329: \tdefer done()\n330: \n331: \tmodelConfigInfo := types.ModelConfigInfo{\n332: \t\tProvider: *providerConfig, // shallow copy\n333: \t\tModel:    *modelConfig,    // shallow copy\n334: \t}\n335: \n336: \t// Finally! With all the necessary information we can now create the CompletionsClient for\n337: \t// contacting the LLM and responding to the request.\n338: \t// Combine base scope with ScopeComponent (e.g., \"chat.deepsearch\" + \"finder\" = \"chat.deepsearch.finder\")\n339: \tfinalScope := string(h.scope)\n340: \tif params.ScopeComponent != \"\" {\n341: \t\tfinalScope = finalScope + \".\" + params.ScopeComponent\n342: \t}\n343: \tcompletionClient, err := client.Get(\n344: \t\tctx,\n345: \t\th.logger,\n346: \t\tfinalScope,\n347: \t\tmodelConfigInfo,\n348: \t)\n349: \tl := trace.Logger(ctx, h.logger)\n350: \tif err != nil {\n351: \t\treturn &errcode.HTTPErr{\n352: \t\t\tStatus: http.StatusInternalServerError,\n353: \t\t\tErr:    err,\n354: \t\t}\n355: \t}\n356: \n357: \t// Check rate limit.\n358: \terr = h.rl.TryAcquire(ctx)\n359: \tif err != nil {\n360: \t\tif unwrap, ok := err.(types.RateLimitExceededError); ok {\n361: \t\t\treturn &unwrap\n362: \t\t}\n363: \t\tl.Warn(\"Rate limit error\", log.Error(err))\n364: \n365: \t\treturn &errcode.HTTPErr{\n366: \t\t\tStatus: http.StatusInternalServerError,\n367: \t\t\tErr:    errors.New(\"Internal server error\"),\n368: \t\t}\n369: \t}\n370: \n371: \t// Assemble the full completion request.\n372: \tfullCompletionRequest := h.getFullCompletionRequest(request, params, modelConfigInfo, currentModelConfig.SystemPreInstruction)\n373: \n374: \t// Check for cody_debug command\n375: \tdebugResult := checkForDebugCommand(*fullCompletionRequest)\n376: \tif debugResult.IsDebugCommand {\n377: \t\t// Only allow site admins to use debug features\n378: \t\t// For non-admins, just ignore the debug command silently and continue with normal processing\n379: \t\tif err := sgauth.CheckCurrentUserIsSiteAdmin(ctx, h.db); err != nil {\n380: \t\t\th.logger.Debug(\"non-admin user used debug command, ignoring silently\", log.Error(err))\n381: \t\t\t// Fall through to normal processing below\n382: \t\t} else {\n383: \t\t\t// User is admin, process the debug command\n384: \n385: \t\t\t// If there's an error in the debug command syntax, return it to the user\n386: \t\t\tif debugResult.ErrorMessage != \"\" {\n387: \t\t\t\th.logger.Info(\"Debug command syntax error\", log.String(\"error\", debugResult.ErrorMessage))\n388: \n389: \t\t\t\t// Use the normal streaming response infrastructure to send the error\n390: \t\t\t\tif request.IsStream(h.feature) {\n391: \t\t\t\t\treturn serveStreamingResponse(\n392: \t\t\t\t\t\tsink, ctx, h.logger,\n393: \t\t\t\t\t\t*fullCompletionRequest, &errorCompletionClient{errorMessage: debugResult.ErrorMessage},\n394: \t\t\t\t\t\th.grAttributionTest, h.auditLog, handlerStart)\n395: \t\t\t\t} else {\n396: \t\t\t\t\tserveSyncResponse(\n397: \t\t\t\t\t\tsink, ctx, h.logger,\n398: \t\t\t\t\t\t*fullCompletionRequest, &errorCompletionClient{errorMessage: debugResult.ErrorMessage},\n399: \t\t\t\t\t\th.auditLog, handlerStart)\n400: \t\t\t\t}\n401: \t\t\t\treturn nil\n402: \t\t\t}\n403: \n404: \t\t\t// Run the latency test\n405: \t\t\tif request.IsStream(h.feature) {\n406: \t\t\t\treturn serveStreamingResponse(\n407: \t\t\t\t\tsink, ctx, h.logger,\n408: \t\t\t\t\tdebugResult.ModifiedRequest, &latencyTestClient{\n409: \t\t\t\t\t\toriginalClient: completionClient,\n410: \t\t\t\t\t\ttestCount:      debugResult.LatencyTest,\n411: \t\t\t\t\t\tlogger:         h.logger,\n412: \t\t\t\t\t}, h.grAttributionTest, h.auditLog, handlerStart)\n413: \t\t\t} else {\n414: \t\t\t\tserveSyncResponse(\n415: \t\t\t\t\tsink, ctx, h.logger,\n416: \t\t\t\t\tdebugResult.ModifiedRequest, &latencyTestClient{\n417: \t\t\t\t\t\toriginalClient: completionClient,\n418: \t\t\t\t\t\ttestCount:      debugResult.LatencyTest,\n419: \t\t\t\t\t\tlogger:         h.logger,\n420: \t\t\t\t\t}, h.auditLog, handlerStart)\n421: \t\t\t}\n422: \t\t\treturn nil\n423: \t\t}\n424: \t}\n425: \n426: \tif request.IsStream(h.feature) {\n427: \t\treturn serveStreamingResponse(\n428: \t\t\tsink, ctx, h.logger,\n429: \t\t\t*fullCompletionRequest, completionClient, h.grAttributionTest, h.auditLog, handlerStart)\n430: \t}\n431: \tserveSyncResponse(\n432: \t\tsink, ctx, h.logger,\n433: \t\t*fullCompletionRequest, completionClient, h.auditLog, handlerStart)\n434: \n435: \treturn nil\n436: }\n437: \n438: func (h *CompletionsHandler) getFullCompletionRequest(request types.CodyCompletionRequestParameters, params types.InternalCompletionParams, modelConfigInfo types.ModelConfigInfo, systemPreInstruction string) *types.CompletionRequest {\n439: \t// Assemble the full completion request.\n440: \tfullCompletionRequest := types.CompletionRequest{\n441: that the capabilities requested in the completion params are available in the requested model\n457: func validateRequestCapabilities(request types.CodyCompletionRequestParameters, params types.InternalCompletionParams, modelConfig *modelconfigtypes.Model, logger log.Logger, feature types.CompletionsFeature, scope Scope) error {\n458: \t{\n459: \t\t// Validate the vision capability\n460: \t\tvisionCapabilityUsed := usesVisionCapability(request)\n461: \t\t// NOTE: dotcom models have no capabilities due to CODY-3800, so\n462: \t\t// we're going to reject all vision %s does not support the vision capability. To fix this problem, remove the message content of type image_url or change the requested model.\", modelConfig.ModelRef),\n468: \t\t\t\tStatus: http.StatusBadRequest,\n469: \t\t\t}\n470: \t\t}\n471: \n472: \t\tif visionCapabilityUsed && !visionEnabled(scope) {\n473: \t\t\tlogger.Warn(\"vision capability is not enabled for this instance\", log.String(\"model\", string(modelConfig.ModelRef)))\n474: \t\t\treturn &errcode.HTTPErr{\n475: \t\t\t\tErr:    errors.New(\"vision capability is not enabled for this instance. writeErr != nil {\n544: \t\t\tl.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"error reporting %s error\", feature), log.Error(writeErr))\n545: \t\t}\n546: \t}\n547: \treturn errorReporters{\n548: \t\tstreaming:   func(err error) { report(err, \"error\", \"streaming completion\") },\n549: \t\tattribution: func(err error) { report(err, \"attribution-error\", \"attribution\") },\n550: \t}\n551: }\n552: \n553: // serveStreamingResponse handles streaming requests to an LLM provider,\n554: // It writes events to an SSE stream as they come in.\n555: func serveStreamingResponse(\n556: \tsink types.CompletionsSink,\n557: \tctx context.Context, logger log.Logger,\n558: \tcompRequest types.CompletionRequest, cc types.CompletionsClient,\n559: \ttest guardrails.AttributionTest, auditLog codyauditlog.Service,\n560: \thandlerStart time.Time,\n561: ) error {\n562: \tstreamer := sink.NewStreamSink()\n563: \tif streamer == nil {\n564: \t\treturn nil\n565: \t}\n566: \tdeferred := streamer.Deferred()\n567: \tif deferred != nil {\n568: \t\tdefer deferred()\n569: \t}\n570: \n571: \terrorReporters := newErrorReporters(ctx, logger, streamer)\n572: \n573: \tf := guardrails.NoopCompletionsFilter(streamer.Handle)\n574: \tif cf := conf.GetConfigFeatures(conf.SiteConfig()); cf != nil && cf.Attribution &&\n575: \t\tfeatureflag.FromContext(ctx).GetBoolOr(\"autocomplete-attribution\", true) {\n576: \t\tfactory := guardrails.NewCompletionsFilter\n577: \t\t// TODO(#61828) - Validate & cleanup:\n578: \t\t// 1.  If experiments are successful on S2 and we do not see any panics,\n579: \t\t//     please switch the feature flag default value to true.\n580: \t\t// 2.  Afterwards cleanup the implementation and only use V2 completion filter.\n581: \t\t//     Remove v1 implementation completely.\n582: \t\tif featureflag.FromContext(ctx).GetBoolOr(\"autocomplete-attribution-v2\", false) {\n583: \t\t\tfactory = guardrails.NewCompletionsFilter2\n584: \t\t}\n585: \t\tff, err := factory(guardrails.CompletionsFilterConfig{\n586: \t\t\tSink:             streamer.Handle,\n587: \t\t\tTest:             test,\n588: \t\t\tAttributionError: errorReporters.attribution,\n589: \t\t})\n590: \t\tif err != nil {\n591: \t\t\terrorReporters.attribution(err)\n592: \t\t} else {\n593: \t\t\tf = ff\n594: \t\t}\n595: \t}\n596: \n597: \tdeltaText := []string{}\n598: \tresponse := &types.CompletionResponse{}\n599: \n600: \t// Track approximate start time of upstream LLM request. This timestamp is captured right before\n601: \t// calling cc.Stream(), so it's very close to when the actual upstream request begins.\n602: \tupstreamReqStart := time.Now()\n603: \tvar onlyOnFirstEvent sync.Once\n604: \t// Build and send the completions request.\n605: \tsendEventFn := func(event types.CompletionResponse) error {\n606: \t\t// Some of the LLM backends send empty chunks that we skip forwarding to\n607: \t\t// the client.  It's more reliable to do this check once here instead of\n608: \t\t// having every LLM backend do this validation, which is easy to forget.\n609: \t\t// The chat client crashes with the  error below when the `completion`\n610: \t\t// property is missing:\n611: \t\t//     \"Request Failed: Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'length')\"\n612: \t\tif event.IsEmpty() {\n613: \t\t\treturn nil\n614: \t\t}\n615: \t\tif auditLog != nil {\n616: \t\t\tdeltaText = append(deltaText, event.DeltaText)\n617: \t\t\tif len(event.Completion) > 0 {\n618: \t\t\t\tresponse.Completion = event.Completion\n619: \t\t\t} else if len(event.DeltaText) > 0 {\n620: \t\t\t\tdeltaText = append(deltaText, event.DeltaText)\n621: \t\t\t}\n622: \t\t\tif event.Model != nil {\n623: \t\t\t\tresponse.Model = event.Model\n624: \t\t\t\t// Record in the response what \"modelref\" (Sourcegraph canonical\n625: \t\t\t\t// representation) was used in this request. This is required to\n626: \t\t\t\t// correctly estimate the cost of the completion.\n627: \t\t\t\tif event.ModelRef == nil {\n628: \t\t\t\t\tresponse.ModelRef = new(string(compRequest.ModelConfigInfo.Model.ModelRef))\n629: \t\t\t\t}\n630: \t\t\t}\n631: \t\t\tif event.Usage != nil {\n632: \t\t\t\tresponse.Usage = event.Usage\n633: \t\t\t}\n634: \t\t}\n635: \t\tonlyOnFirstEvent.Do(func() {\n636: \t\t\ttimeToFirstEventMetrics.Observe(\n637: \t\t\t\ttime.Since(upstreamReqStart).Seconds(),\n638: \t\t\t\t1,\n639: \t\t\t\tnil,\n640: \t\t\t\tstring(compRequest.Feature),\n641: \t\t\t\tstring(compRequest.ModelConfigInfo.Model.ModelRef.ProviderID()),\n642: \t\t\t\tstring(compRequest.ModelConfigInfo.Model.ModelRef.ModelID()),\n643: \t\t\t)\n644: \t\t})\n645: \n646: \t\treturn f.Send(ctx, event)\n647: \t}\n648: \n649: \t// Record the time taken for initial request processing overhead before sending to the LLM provider.\n650: \tcompletionsHandlerOverheadMetrics.Observe(\n651: \t\ttime.Since(handlerStart).Seconds(),\n652: \t\t1,\n653: \t\tnil,\n654: \t\tstring(compRequest.Feature),\n655: \t\tstring(compRequest.ModelConfigInfo.Model.ModelRef.ProviderID()),\n656: \t\tstring(compRequest.ModelConfigInfo.Model.ModelRef.ModelID()),\n657: \t)\n658: \n659: \terr := cc.Stream(ctx, logger, compRequest, sendEventFn)\n660: \tif err != nil {\n661: \t\tl := trace.Logger(ctx, logger)\n662: \t\tlogFields := []log.Field{log.Error(err)}\n663: \n664: \t\tstreamer.FatalError(ctx, l, err)\n665: \t\tif errNotOK, ok := types.IsErrStatusNotOK(err); ok {\n666: \t\t\tif tc := errNotOK.SourceTraceContext; tc != nil {\n667: \t\t\t\tlogFields = append(logFields,\n668: \t\t\t\t\tlog.String(\"sourceTraceContext.traceID\", tc.TraceID),\n669: \t\t\t\t\tlog.String(\"sourceTraceContext.spanID\", tc.SpanID))\n670: \t\t\t}\n671: \t\t}\n672: \n673: \t\tif errors.IsAny(err, context.Canceled, context.DeadlineExceeded) {\n674: \t\t\tl.Warn(\"canceled while streaming completions\", logFields...)\n675: \t\t} else {\n676: \t\t\tl.Error(\"error while streaming completions\", logFields...)\n677: \t\t}\n678: \n679: \t\t// Note that we do NOT attempt to forward the status code to the\n680: \t\t// client here, since we are using streamhttp.Writer - see\n681: \t\t// streamhttp.NewWriter for more details. Instead, we send an error\n682: \t\t// event, which clients should check as appropriate.\n683: \t\terrorReporters.streaming(err)\n684: \t\t// For internal callers, we propgate the error so it can be handled upstream\n685: \t\treturn err\n686: \t}\n687: \tif f != nil { // if autocomplete-attribution enabled\n688: \t\tif err := f.WaitDone(ctx); err != nil {\n689: \t\t\terrorReporters.streaming(err)\n690: \t\t}\n691: \t}\n692: \n693: \tif auditLog != nil && response != nil {\n694: \t\tif len(response.Completion) == 0 {\n695: \t\t\tresponse.Completion = strings.Join(deltaText, \"\")\n696: \t\t}\n697: \n698: \t\t// We still want to auditlog even if the user canceled the request.\n699: \t\tctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.WithoutCancel(ctx), 10*time.Second)\n700: \t\tdefer cancel()\n701: \n702: \t\taddAuditLogEntry(ctx, logger, auditLog, compRequest, *response)\n703: \t}\n704: \treturn nil\n705: }\n706: \n707: // serveSyncResponse handles non-streaming requests to an LLM provider,\n708: // awaiting the complete response before writing it back in a structured JSON response\n709: // to the client.\n710: func serveSyncResponse(\n711: \tsink types.CompletionsSink,\n712: \tctx context.Context, logger log.Logger,\n713: \tcompRequest types.CompletionRequest, cc types.CompletionsClient,\n714: \tauditLog codyauditlog.Service,\n715: \thandlerStart time.Time,\n716: ) {\n717: \t// Record the time taken for initial request processing overhead before sending to LLM.\n718: \tcompletionsHandlerOverheadMetrics.Observe(\n719: \t\ttime.Since(handlerStart).Seconds(),\n720: \t\t1,\n721: \t\tnil,\n722: \t\tstring(compRequest.Feature),\n723: \t\tstring(compRequest.ModelConfigInfo.Model.ModelRef.ProviderID()),\n724: \t\tstring(compRequest.ModelConfigInfo.Model.ModelRef.ModelID()),\n725: \t)\n726: \tcompletion, err := cc.Complete(ctx, logger, compRequest)\n727: \n728: \tif err != nil {\n729: \t\tsink.SyncResponseError(ctx, err)\n730: \t\treturn\n731: \t}\n732: \n733: \tif completion == nil {\n734: \t\tsink.SyncResponseError(ctx, errors.New(\"no completion\"))\n735: \t\treturn\n736: \t}\n737: \n738: \tif completion.ModelRef == nil {\n739: \t\t// Record in the response what \"modelref\" (Sourcegraph canonical\n740: \t\t// representation) was used in this request. This is required to\n741: \t\t// correctly estimate the cost of the completion.\n742: \t\tcompletion.ModelRef = new(string(compRequest.ModelConfigInfo.Model.ModelRef))\n743: \t}\n744: \n745: \t// On older versions of the completions API, we don't include the usage\n746: \tif compRequest.Version < types.CompletionsV5 {\n747: \t\tcompletion.Usage = nil\n748: \t\tcompletion.Model = nil\n749: *completion)\n756: \n757: \tif auditLog != nil {\n758: \t\taddAuditLogEntry(ctx, logger, auditLog, compRequest, *completion)\n759: \t}\n760: }\n761: \n762: func newCodyIgnoreCompatibilityError(reason string, statusCode int) *errcode.HTTPErr {\n763: \tconst prefix = \"ClientCodyIgnoreCompatibilityError\"\n764: \treturn &errcode.HTTPErr{Status: statusCode, Err: errors.Newf(\"%s: %s\", prefix, reason)}\n765: }\n766: \n767: // checkClientCodyIgnoreCompatibility checks if the client version respects Cody context filters (aka Cody Ignore) defined in the site config.\n768: // A non-nil codyIgnoreCompatibilityError implies that the HTTP request should be rejected with the error text and code from the returned error.\n769: // Error text is safe to be surfaced to end user.\n770: func checkClientCodyIgnoreCompatibility(ctx context.Context, db database.DB, client types.ClientInformation) error {\n771: \t// If Cody context filters are not defined on the instance, we do not restrict client version.\n772: \t// Because the site hasn't configured Cody Ignore, no need to enforce it.\n773: \tif conf.SiteConfig().CodyContextFilters == nil {\n774: \t\treturn nil\n775: \t}\n776: \n777: \t}\n783: \n784: \t// If cody-context-filters-clients-test-mode feature flag is enabled, the client version constaint\n785: \t// allows pre-release versions (see https://pkg.go.dev/github.com/Masterminds/semver#readme-working-with-pre-release-versions).\n786: \t// Intended for development use only.\n787: \tflag, err := db.FeatureFlags().GetFeatureFlag(ctx, \"cody-context-filters-clients-test-mode\")\n788: \tif err != nil && !errors.Is(err, sql.ErrNoRows) {\n789: \t\treturn newCodyIgnoreCompatibilityError(\n790: \t\t\t\"Failed to get feature flag the user is authenticated.\n53: \ta := actor.FromContext(ctx)\n54: \tif a.IsInternal() {\n55: \t\treturn nil\n56: \t}\n57: \tkey := userKey(a.UID, r.scope)\n58: \tif !a.IsAuthenticated() {\n59: \t\t// Fall back to the IP address, if provided in context (ie. this is a request handler).\n60: \t\treq := requestclient.FromContext(ctx)\n61: \t\tvar ip string\n62: \t\tif req != nil {\n63: \t\t\tip = req.IP\n64: \t\t\t// Note: ForwardedFor header in general can be spoofed. For\n65: \t\t\t// Sourcegraph.com we use a trusted value for this so this is a\n66: \t\t\t// reliable value to rate limit with.\n67: \t\t\tif req.ForwardedFor != \"\" {\n68: \t\t\t\tip = req.ForwardedFor\n69: \t\t\t}\n70: \t\t}\n71: \t\tif ip == \"\" {\n72: \t\t\treturn errors.Wrap(auth.ErrNotAuthenticated, \"cannot claim rate limit for unauthenticated user without request context\")\n73: \t\t}\n74: \t\tkey = anonymousKey(ip, r.scope)\n75: \t}\n76: \n77: \t// Check the current usage. If\n78: \t// no record exists, redis will return 0 and ErrNil.\n79: \tcurrentUsage, err := r.rstore.Get(ctx, key).Int()\n80: \tif err != nil && err != keyvalue.ErrNil {\n81: \t\treturn errors.Wrap(err, \"failed to read rate limit counter\")\n82: \t}\n83: \n84: \t// If the usage exceeds the maximum, we return an error. Consumers can check if\n85: \t// the error is of type RateLimitExceededError and extract additional information\n86: \t// like the limit and the time by when they should retry.\n87: \tif currentUsage >= limit {\n88: \t\t// Read TTL to compute the RetryAfter time.\n89: \t\tttl, err := r.rstore.TTL(ctx, key)\n90: \t\tif err != nil {\n91: \t\t\treturn errors.Wrap(err, \"failed to get TTL for rate limit counter\")\n92: \t\t}\n93: \t\treturn types.RateLimitExceededError{\n94: \t\t\tScope: r.scope,\n95: \t\t\tLimit: limit,\n96: \t\t\t// Return the minimum value of currentUsage and limit to not return\n97: \t\t\t// confusing values when the limit was exceeded. This method increases\n98: \t\t\t// on every check, even if the limit was reached.\n99: \t\t\tUsed:       min(currentUsage, limit),\n100: \t\t\tRetryAfter: time.Now().Add(time.Duration(ttl) * time.Second),\n101: \t\t}\n102: \t}\n103: \n104: \t// Now that we know that we want to let the user pass, let's increment the rate\n105: \t// limit counter for the user.\n106: \t// Note that the rate limiter _may_ allow slightly more requests than the configured\n107: \t// limit, incrementing the rate limit counter and reading the usage futher up are currently\n108: \t// not an atomic operation, because there is no good way to read the TTL in a transaction\n109: \t// without a lua script.\n110: \t// This approach could also slightly overcount the usage if redis requests after\n111: \t// the INCR fail, but it will always recover safely.\n112: \t// If Incr works but then everything else fails (eg ctx cancelled) the user spent\n113: \t// a token without getting anything for it. This seems pretty rare and a fine trade-off\n114: \t// since its just one token. The most likely reason this would happen is user cancelling\n115: \t// the request and at that point its more likely to happen while the LLM is running than\n116: \t// in this quick redis block.\n117: \t// On the first request in the current time block, if the requests past Incr fail we don't\n118: \t// yet have a deadline set. This means if the user comes back later we wouldn't of expired\n119: \t// just one token. This seems fine. Note: this isn't an issue on subsequent requests in the\n120: \t// same time block since the TTL would have been set.\n121: \n122: \tif _, err := r.rstore.Incr(ctx, key); err != nil {\n123: \t\treturn errors.Wrap(err, \"failed to increment rate limit counter\")\n124: \t}\n125: \n126: \t// Set expiry on the key. If the key didn't exist prior to the previous INCR,\n127: \t// it will set the expiry of the key to one day.\n128: \t// If it did exist before, it should have an expiry set already, so the TTL >= 0\n129: \t// makes sure that we don't overwrite it and restart the 1h bucket.\n130: \tttl, err := r.rstore.TTL(ctx, key)\n131: \tif err != nil {\n132: \t\treturn errors.Wrap(err, \"failed to get TTL for rate limit counter\")\n133: \t}\n134: \tif ttl < 0 {\n135: \t\tif err := r.rstore.Expire(ctx, key, int(24*time.Hour/time.Second)); err != nil {\n136: \t\t\treturn errors.Wrap(err, \"failed to set expiry for rate limit counter\")\n137: \t\t}\n138: \t}\n139: \n140: \treturn nil\n141: }\n142: \n143: func userKey(userID int32, scope types.CompletionsFeature) string {\n144: \treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"user:%d:%s_requests\", userID, scope)\n145: }\n146: \n147: func anonymousKey(ip string, scope types.CompletionsFeature) string {\n148: \treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"anon:%s:%s_requests\", ip, scope)\n149: }\n150: \n151: func getConfiguredLimit(ctx context.Context, db database.DB, gp gating.Provider, scope types.CompletionsFeature) (int, error) {\n152: \ta := actor.FromContext(ctx)\n153: There is\\n43: // a super-important detail here! Typically, \\\"Provider\\\" is referring to the \\\"Model Provider\\\". Or\\n44: // a 3rd party that built various models. The \\\"API Provider\\\" on the other hand is the actual API\\n45: // or service we use to make LLM requests. And the two may be very different.\\n46: //\\n47: // For example, the Model Provider may be \\\"openai\\\" but the API Provider could be Cody Gateway,\\n48: // AzureOpenAI, or even AWS Bedrock.\\n49: //\\n50: // So the `modelConfigInfo.Provider` isn't strictly necessary. We don't care _who built_ the model,\\n51: // instead we care about the API we need to call in order to serve the request. So we look at the\\n52: // `modelConfigInfo.Provider.ServerSideConfig` to determine which CompletionsClient should be used\\n53: // to make the actual LLM request.\\n54: func getAPIProvider(ctx context.Context, modelConfigInfo types.ModelConfigInfo, traceFamily string) (types.CompletionsClient, error) {\\n55: \\t// TODO(sayans/emidoots): right now it looks like a new client is being created every time; they are not being cached.\\n56: \\t// This is bad, we should cache the clients. Then it serves either a streaming or synchronous response depending on the request type.\n\n**Layer 3: Completions Client (Provider Selection)**\n- `internal/completions/client/client.go` - `Get()`, Gateway)\n- `internal/completions/client/codygateway/codygateway.go` - `NewClient()`, `clientForParams()`, `gatewayDoer()`\n  - Adds authentication headers, feature headers for tracking, and scope headers for tracing before forwarding to the gateway\n\n**Layer 4: Cody Gateway Service**\n- `cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/handler.go` - Gateway HTTP handler registration\n  - Middleware chain: latency → interaction-tracking → instrumentation → auth → request logger → handler\n- The auth middleware validates tokens against enterprise subscriptions and workspaces, returning appropriate status codes for unauthorized or forbidden access\n- The rate limiting middleware then checks per-feature limits for the actor and returns 429 if exceeded\n- The upstream handler validates the feature Sourcegraph frontend and Cody Gateway — with rate limiting enforced at multiple layers.\\n\\n**Layer 1 — GraphQL Entry Point (Frontend)**\\nThe `Completions` GraphQL mutation is defined in `cmd/frontend/graphqlbackend/completions.go` and implemented by `completionsResolver` in `cmd/frontend/internal/completions/resolvers/resolver.go`. On entry it: (1) calls `completionsapis.IsEnabled` (which delegates to `cody.IsCodyEnabled`) to check if the feature is enabled; (2) resolves the default chat/fast-chat model via `modelconfig.Get()`; (3) checks the per-user Redis-backed rate limit via `rateLimiter.TryAcquire`; then (4) calls `client.Get()` → `client.Complete()` to produce the completion.\\n\\n**Layer 2 — HTTP API Handlers (Frontend)**\\nFor HTTP Cody API clients (VS Code, JetBrains), requests hit `/.api/completions/stream` (chat) or `/.api/completions/code`, handled by `CompletionsHandler.ServeHTTP` in `cmd/frontend/internal/httpapi/completions/handler.go`. The handler enforces: (a) completions-enabled check; (b) client version/CodyIgnore compatibility guard; (c) model resolution and capability validation (vision, tools); (d) another Redis-backed per-user/per-IP rate limiter via `h.rl.TryAcquire` using `limiter.go`. The rate limiter reads a per-user daily quota override from the database (`db.Users().GetChatCompletionsQuota`) or falls back to the global `completions.perUserDailyLimit` site config. Exceeded limits produce 429 responses with `x-ratelimit-limit`, `x-ratelimit-remaining`, and `retry-after` headers.\\n\\n**Layer 3 — Provider Selection (Frontend Client)**\\n`internal/completions/client/client.go:getAPIProvider` inspects `provider.ServerSideConfig` to pick the correct backend client: AWSBedrock, AzureOpenAI, OpenAICompatible, Anthropic (direct), Google (direct), GenericProvider (Fireworks or OpenAI direct), or SourcegraphProvider (Cody Gateway). When the provider is `SourcegraphProvider`, `codygateway.NewClient` is instantiated, which builds a `gatewayDoer` that injects auth headers (via `auther.Authenticate`) and sets the `X-Sourcegraph-Feature` and `X-Sourcegraph-Scope` headers before proxying the request to Cody Gateway.\\n\\n**Layer 4 — Cody Gateway Auth (Middleware)**\\nAt Cody Gateway, the `registerStandardEndpoint` wrapper in `cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/handler.go` stacks: latency → interaction-tracking → instrumentation → `authr.Middleware` → request-logger → handler. `auth.Authenticator.Middleware` (in `cmd/cody-gateway/internal/auth/auth.go`) calls `Sources.Get(ctx, r.Header)` to resolve the caller into a Gateway `Actor` by trying each registered actor source (enterprise subscriptions, workspaces, dotcom users). Failures produce 401 (credentials denied/unrecognized), 403 (actor forbidden/access disabled), or 503 (upstream error). A successful auth stores the `Actor` in context.\\n\\n**Layer 5 — Cody Gateway Feature Rate Limiting**\\n`featurelimiter.Handle` (in `cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/featurelimiter/featurelimiter.go`) extracts the feature from the `X-Sourcegraph-Feature` header, then calls `act.Limiter(ctx, logger, cache, feature, rateLimitNotifier)` to get the actor's per-feature Redis limiter, followed by `l.TryAcquire`. Rate limits are stored on the actor (`Actor.RateLimits map[Feature]RateLimit`) and come from the actor source (e.g. the enterprise subscription's configured limits). Exceeding the limit fires a `rate_limited` event log and returns 429 with `retry-after`. This is the layer most likely to produce 429s for legitimate but high-volume customers.\\n\\n**Layer 6 — Upstream Handler (Cody Gateway → LLM Provider)**\\n`makeUpstreamHandler` in `cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/completions/upstream.go` performs: request body parsing → abuse/flagging check (`shouldFlagRequest`) → model allowlist validation (`isAllowedModel` against embedded model config) → model availability circuit-breaker (`modelAvailabilityTracker`) → request transformation and proxying to the upstream LLM API. If the upstream itself returns 429, it is rewritten to 503 (to prevent clients from naively retrying) and a `retry-after` header is forwarded or defaulted. Provider-specific handlers (Anthropic, Fireworks, OpenAI, Google) live in `cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/completions/` and each implement `upstreamHandlerMethods`.\\n\\n**429 Root Causes Summary**\\n1. Frontend per-user daily rate limit exceeded (Redis counter in `limiter.go`) → 429 with `rate_limit_exceeded` JSON error code.\\n2. Cody Gateway actor feature rate limit exceeded (`featurelimiter.HandleFeature`) → 429 from Gateway.\\n3. Upstream LLM provider rate limit (TPM/RPM quota exhausted) → rewritten by Gateway to 503 with `retry-after`; clients may misinterpret this as a 429 if they observe the original upstream headers.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1864,"cache_read_input_tokens":92785,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1864,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":8,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4c223356-dc30-4874-9d4f-2eeb8285ffdf","uuid":"1a594ad5-73c6-426c-9ab7-11ab47f781c6"}

Failures produce 401 (credentials denied/unrecognized), 403 (actor forbidden/access disabled), or 503 (upstream error). Success stores the `Actor` in context.\\n\\n**Layer 5 — Cody Gateway Feature Rate Limiting**\\n`featurelimiter.Handle` in `cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/featurelimiter/featurelimiter.go` extracts the feature from the `X-Sourcegraph-Feature` header, then calls `act.Limiter(ctx, logger, cache, feature, rateLimitNotifier)` to get the actor's per-feature Redis limiter, followed by `l.TryAcquire`. Rate limits are stored on the actor (`Actor.RateLimits map[Feature]RateLimit`) and sourced from the actor's enterprise subscription configuration. Exceeding the limit fires a `rate_limited` event log and returns HTTP 429 with a `retry-after` header. This is the layer most likely to produce intermittent 429s for legitimate high-volume customers.\\n\\n**Layer 6 — Upstream Handler (Cody Gateway -> LLM Provider)**\\n`makeUpstreamHandler` in `cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/completions/upstream.go` performs: request body parsing -> abuse/flagging check (`shouldFlagRequest`) -> model allowlist validation (`isAllowedModel` against embedded model config) -> model availability circuit-breaker (`modelAvailabilityTracker`, which blocks requests to models with recent 429s or timeouts) -> request transformation and proxying to the upstream LLM API. If the upstream itself returns 429, it is rewritten to 503 (to prevent clients from naively retrying) and a `retry-after` header is forwarded or defaulted to 30 seconds. Provider-specific handlers (Anthropic, Fireworks, OpenAI, Google) live in `cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/completions/` and each implement the `upstreamHandlerMethods` interface.\\n\\n**429 Root Causes Summary**\\n1. Frontend per-user daily quota exceeded (Redis counter in `limiter.go`, checked in `ProcessCompletion`) -> HTTP 429 with JSON error code `rate_limit_exceeded`.\\n2. Cody Gateway actor feature rate limit exceeded (`featurelimiter.HandleFeature`) -> HTTP 429 from Gateway before the request reaches the LLM.\\n3. Upstream LLM provider quota exhausted (TPM/RPM limit) -> Gateway rewrites upstream 429 to HTTP 503 with `retry-after`; the `modelAvailabilityTracker` also blocks subsequent requests to that model temporarily.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1354,"cache_read_input_tokens":101435,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1354,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4c223356-dc30-4874-9d4f-2eeb8285ffdf","uuid":"e577d488-81e1-406f-9f03-8e0e2528098e"}

The resolver checks if completions are enabled, resolves the model config, **checks a Redis rate limit** (`TryAcquire`), then calls `client.Complete()`.\n\n### Layer 2 — HTTP API Handlers\n`CompletionsHandler.ServeHTTP` in `cmd/frontend/internal/httpapi/completions/handler.go` serves `/.api/completions/stream` (chat) and `/.api/completions/code`. It enforces:\n- **Completions-enabled check** (`checkCompletionsEnabled` → `cody.IsCodyEnabled`)\n- **Client version/CodyIgnore compatibility** (`checkClientCodyIgnoreCompatibility`)\n- **Model capability validation** (vision, tools)\n- **Per-user Redis rate limit** via `limiter.go` — reads per-user DB quota override, falls back to global `perUserDailyLimit` site config; returns HTTP 429 on excess\n\n### Layer 3 — Provider Selection\n`internal/completions/client/client.go:getAPIProvider` picks among 7 backend clients based on `ServerSideConfig`: AWSBedrock, AzureOpenAI, OpenAICompatible, Anthropic (direct), Google (direct), GenericProvider (Fireworks/OpenAI), or **SourcegraphProvider (Cody Gateway)**. When Cody Gateway is selected, `gatewayDoer` injects auth headers and `X-Sourcegraph-Feature`.\n\n### Layer 4 — Cody Gateway Auth\n`cmd/cody-gateway/internal/auth/auth.go:Authenticator.Middleware` calls `Sources.Get()` to resolve the bearer token into an `Actor` (enterprise subscription, workspace, or dotcom user). Returns 401/403/503 on failure.\n\n### Layer 5 — Gateway Feature Rate Limiting\n`cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/featurelimiter/featurelimiter.go:HandleFeature` reads the actor's per-feature `RateLimits` and calls `l.TryAcquire()` against Redis. **This is the most likely source of intermittent 429s** for legitimate customers — returns HTTP 429 with `retry-after`.\n\n### Layer 6 — Upstream Handler → LLM Provider\n`cmd/cody-gateway/internal/httpapi/completions/upstream.go:makeUpstreamHandler` validates the model against an allowlist, checks a **model availability circuit-breaker** (blocks models with recent 429s/timeouts), then proxies to Anthropic/Fireworks/OpenAI/Google.
